data 
  
Indsamling af data 
 
Bredde 
Alt baseret på egen 
erfaring 
(tegning) 
noter: perspektiver, 
“viewpoints” snæver 
Har interviewet en 
fra målgruppen 
Bredt overblik over 
målgruppe (flere 
interviews) 
Har interviewet 
udpluk fra alle 
relevante 
stakeholders 
Har interviewet adskillige 
folk fra målgruppe, og alle 
andre (kendte) relevante 
stakeholders 
Note: bredspektret data 
Kvalitet af 
interviews 
(interview 
teknikker fx) 
“Skal den være rød eller 
blå?” abstraktionsniveau 
 
Indsigter er farvede af 
ledende 
spørgsmål/priming 
 
Åbne spørgsmål -> 
ufarvede 
problem/kontekstorienter
ede 
Indsigter draget på 
data 
exploratory vs. 
confirmatory 
Indsigter baseret på 
“hvad vil du ha’?” 
spørgsmål 
 
 
 
Alle er confident med at 
oversætte svar og 
holdninger til reelle 
indsigter 
Databrug i 
beslutningstagning 
“statistikken siger x% 
køber y-produkter, så…” 
-> fokus på potentielt 
marked frem for reelle 
indsigter 
(eller 100% 
mavefornemmelse) 
 
 
 
Indsigter er defineret ud 
fra gode interviews med en 
substantiel mængde 
stakeholders og 
beslutnnger drages på 
reelle, dokumenterede 
indsigter 
Kreativitet 
Kreativ selvtillid 
 
Ingen føler sig 
kreative 
 
Vi kan godt få idéer, 
men vi kan ikke 
omsætte dem til 
virkelighed 
 
 
Alle tror på at de kan 
bidrage positivt, gøre en 
forskel, være kreative og 
skabe bedre løsninger og 
få reel indflydelse

Metoder 
 
Metodebevidsthed 
og brug 
Metoderne er ukendt 
for mig 
Jeg kender til metoder,  
A) 
og har prøvet dem i 
faciliteret forløb 
B) Men har ikke prøvet 
dem 
Jeg har selv brugt 
metoderne i 
arbejdet/et forløb  
(men følger stadig en 
“opskrift”) 
Jeg ved hvilken metode 
jeg skal bruge, og 
hvornår.  
*Høj bevidsthed  
vi italesætter det 
#Rutineret 
Jeg bruger metoder 
ubevidst 
#vi italesætter ikke 
Jeg tilpasser metoder 
Metodebrug 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Åbenhed 
(Divergent) 
Hvor lang tid bruges på 
problemet ift. tid på 
løsning 
Ny formulering 
Når du står med et nyt 
problem hvordan går 
du så til det? 
Vi er ikke bevidste om 
hvad vi gør 
Vi prøver at finde en 
løsning (med det 
samme) 
Vi forstår at vi skal 
undersøge og forstå 
problemet for at finde 
den rigtige løsning  
Vi bruger (lidt) tid på at 
forstå problemet og 
bruger indsigter i 
forhold til at finde 
løsninger 
Vi lægger meget 
arbejde i at undersøge 
problemer og bruger 
systematisk de 
indsigter vi opnår i 
forhold til løsninger 
Vi bevæger os frem og 
tilbage mellem 
problemfeltet og 
løsningsrummet  
Respons på/plads til 
radikale ideer

Menneskecentreret 
data 
  
Indsamling af data 
-
Bredde 
Vi er ikke bevidste om 
at data er vigtigt (når vi 
skal…) 
Vi indsamler ikke data 
fra stakeholders 
Vi indsamler data fra 
én af gruppe ud af alle 
stakeholders 
(vi indsamler data fra 
stakeholders) 
 
 
Vi indsamler data så de 
alle 
stakeholdergrupper er 
repræsenteret i  
(Vi indsamler data så 
de fleste stakeholders 
er repræsenteret) 
Indsamling af data 
-
Systematik 
Vi er ikke bevidste om 
at data er vigtigt (når vi 
skal…) 
Vi har ikke en 
systematisk tilgang til 
indsamling og 
behandling af data 
Vi har en systematisk 
tilgang til indsamling af 
data, men ikke til 
behandling af data 
Vi har en systematisk 
metode(r) til 
indsamling og 
behandling af data 
Vi har en systematisk 
metode(r) til 
indsamling og 
behandling af data OG 
vi ved hvilke data vi 
skal bruge i hver fase 
Vi har en systematisk 
metode(r) til 
indsamling og 
behandling af data OG 
vi ved hvilke data vi 
skal bruge i hver fase 
OG vi forbedrer 
løbende på metoderne. 
Indsamling af data 
-
Objektivitet (i 
spørgsmål) 
Vi er ikke bevidste om 
at data er vigtigt (når vi 
skal…) 
Vi stiller hovedsagelig 
JA/NEJ spørgsmål der 
er nemme at forholde 
sig til 
Vi forstår at man skal 
passe på med farvede 
spørgsmål. Vi har en 
ad-hoc tilgang til at 
udforme spørgsmål 
Vi har en tilgang hvor 
vi stille en kombination 
af åben og ledende 
spørgsmål 
Vi er meget bevidste 
om at stille 
udforskende og 
objektive spørgsmål for 
at undgå at farve data 
Vi er systematiske 
omkring udformning af 
spørgsmål og sørger for 
at de er objektive, 
udforskende. Det virker 
Link mellem data og 
indsigter (tidligere: 
Indsigter draget på 
data)  
Vi er ikke bevidste om 
at data er vigtigt (når vi 
skal…) 
Indsigter er ikke 
baseret på data (eller: 
Vi kan ikke bakke de 
indsigter vi arbejder ud 
fra op med data) 
Vores indsigter er af og 
til baseret på data, men 
ofte er der ikke nogen 
klar sammenhæng 
Vi er enige om at 
indsigter er bedst når 
de er baseret på data og 
vi stræber efter at opnå 
dette 
Indsigter er 
systematisk baseret på 
data og indsigter uden 
rationale drop 
Indsigter er 
systematisk baseret på 
data og indsigter uden 
rationale drop og vi 
forbedrer løbende på 
området 
Databrug i 
beslutningstagning

==PAGE:47==
PARAMETERS 
 
 
 
EXPLANATION 
1 
Method/tool understanding and 
use  
Select suitable methods corresponding to the 
given stage, use them properly and draw valid 
insights from the findings.  
2 
Making ideas tangible or visual 
 
Are the team developing tangible or visuals 
aids/models/prototypes/mockups (in order to 
better understand ideas and support 
communication and the creative process)  
3 
Learning through testing in an 
iterative manner 
How does the team use testing?  
When are hypotheses/ideas tested and how 
systematic are the approach to the testing? 
Are there continuous development from the 
feedback and learnings in an iterative way. 
4 
Mindset awareness 
(Div./Con.) 
How the team works with divergent and 
convergent phases and the problem.  
5 
Width in the data/observations 
gathering 
The extent to which the team collect data that 
represents the relevant stakeholders in the 
right amount.  
6 
Objectivity in the 
data/observations gathering 
The team must be neutral/objective towards 
the people that they are asking (interview, 
survey, focus group..) and towards the 
problem at hand. 
7 
Correlation between 
data/observations and insights 
Are the insights based on data? 
data/observations/information/knowledge 
8 
Correlation between insights and 
solutions 
To what extent have the insights been used in 
the solution? 
9 
Width of ideas (span) 
How broad is the span of ideas in the team’s 
idea generations?  
 
(Innovative/DT) Team culture 
The desired environment for DT 
 This is not a parameter but a headline.  
10 
Diversity in the team (roles and 
responsibility) 
Understanding the need for facilitation, 
“deciders”, “visionaries”, “time keepers” and  
“gate keepers”. To what degree/extent does 
the team contain the needed roles for DT? Are 
all needed roles filled? Is there a hustler, 
hipster and hacker. Are there a leader than 
can be design coach 
11 
Response to radical ideas / Trust 
within the team 
Is there room for radical ideas and thoughts?  
Are every person in the team allowed to 
explore a (crazy) idea that she/he believes in? 
Does every team member feel that they can 
do that? Do they trust the others enough to let 
them do that? 
9Yf iRRI 03q3IRUL3Nj 8j3a rRaGc@RU l
ke
9YfYS
pS ICcj R8 UaL3j3ac
==PAGE:48==
12 
Empathy  
The ability to put yourself in other people's 
place. In order to be able to better understand 
their possibilities and needs.  
13 
Attitude/behaviour towards 
discussion and conflicting views 
The way questions, discussion, disagreement  
are seen. Is it something that the team is open 
towards, or something that should be shot 
down.  
14 
Common language & vocabulary 
Does the team have a common language and 
vocabulary regarding the design process? 
15 
Creative confidence in team 
Do they believe in themselves and are they 
comfortable with making mistakes? 
The ability to think big and act on ideas. Try 
different things without fear of failure. 
16 
Ambiguity 
Is the team aware of and have they embraced 
that they DO NOT KNOW what is going to 
happen and where they end 
17 
Engagement and excitement 
Is everyone equally involved and excited.

Word explanation: insights, design methods, data, design process, divergent/convergent, radical ideas

Understanding and 
use of design 
methods 
 
We have knowledge of 
design methods, and have 
tried to use them in a 
facilitated context OR we 
have not tried to use them. 
We have used design 
methods  in our own work, 
but are still following the 
theory/descriptions closely. 
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
methods to solve specific 
challenges in a 
development process. We 
are vocal and explicit in the 
use of methods as they are 
not entirely ingrained yet. 
 
 
 
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
methods to solve specific 
challenges in a 
development process. We 
use design methods as an 
ingrained and natural part 
of our development 
process.  
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
methods to solve specific 
challenges in a 
development process. We 
use design methods as an 
ingrained and natural part 
of our development 
process. We continuously 
adapt and improve on the 
methods. 
Mindset awareness 
 
We look for a solution 
straight away when we have a 
new problem. 
We understand the 
importance of exploring 
the problem in order to be 
able to find the right 
solution. 
We spend some time to 
understand the problem, 
and then work on solutions. 
We start out by putting a lot 
of effort into exploring the 
problem space and 
afterwards we explore the 
solution space. 
We move freely and 
iteratively between the 
problem and solution 
space.  
 
Width in the 
data/observation 
gathering 
 
We do not gather 
data/observations in a 
structured way. 
We gather most of our 
data/observations from the 
same small group of 
stakeholders as we 
normally do. 
We gather 
data/observations from 
various stakeholder groups. 
 
 
We gather 
data/observations from a 
sensible number of 
stakeholders from all 
relevant stakeholder 
groups.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that we 
gather data/observations 
from a sensible number of 
stakeholders and that all 
relevant stakeholder groups 
are represented. We 
regularly seek out new 
potential stakeholders. 
Width in 
data/observations 
treatment 
 
We are not specific on what 
data treatment method(s) we 
use. We haven’t considered 
whether we use/need 
qualitative or quantitative 
methods. 
We mainly use one data 
treatment method, and 
have considered whether it 
is qualitative or 
quantitative.  
We use a couple of different 
data treatment methods, 
and have considered 
whether it is qualitative or 
quantitative.  
 
We use a combination of 
data treatment methods 
and we make sure that they 
include both qualitative and 
quantitative methods.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that we 
use a well-suited 
combination of data 
treatment methods, 
including both qualitative 
and quantitative methods.  
Preparation to 
data/observation 
gathering 
 
We do not use guidelines for 
how to compose questions 
for data gathering. 
 
 
We have some rules for 
composing questions for 
data gathering, but they are 
not formalised and we don’t 
follow them religiously. 
We have formalised a set of 
guidelines for composing 
questions for data 
gathering. 
We have several methods 
(or a toolbox) for 
composing question for 
data gathering. 
We have several methods 
(or a toolbox) for 
composing question for 
data gathering, which we 
regularly update.

==PAGE:54==
Link between 
insights and 
data/observations  
 
 
Though we have gathered 
data/observations we are not 
able to say exactly how our 
insights are linked with the 
data/observations. 
We are aware that insights 
should be drawn from 
data/observations, but we 
have no approach to ensure 
that they do.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
data/observations. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
data/observations and we 
document the process in 
order to keep track of how 
data/observations and 
insights are linked. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
data/observations and 
continuously improve the 
approach. We document 
throughout the process in 
order to keep track of how 
the data/observations and 
insights are linked.  
 
Tangibility/visualiza
tion of ideas 
 
We rarely use tangible 
and/or visual 
representations of our ideas 
during development. The 
first tangible is the final 
prototype 
We use tangible and/or 
visual representations to 
support communication of 
ideas. 
We sometimes use tangible 
and/or visual 
representations in the 
development process and to 
support communication. 
We normally use tangible 
and/or visual 
representations in synthesis 
work to facilitate discussion 
and development, and to 
support decision making. 
We use tangible and/or 
visual representations as a 
natural part of all synthesis 
work to facilitate discussion 
and development, and to 
support decision making. 
Testing and 
development 
 
We use testing when we have 
developed a more or less 
finished solution. 
We use testing to learn 
before initiating a 
development phase and 
when we have developed a 
more or less finished 
solution.  
We use testing throughout 
the development phase. We 
validate one part of the 
solution at a time and add it 
to the final solution. 
We use testing throughout 
the development phase. We 
validate new parts of the 
solution alone and in 
combination with the entire 
system of the solution.  
We use feedback to 
improve ideas and 
sometimes the fundamental 
concepts. 
We use testing by forming 
hypotheses about the 
solution and testing them 
as cheap and early as 
possible and we use it 
continuously throughout 
the development phase. 
Feedback are seen as 
learning points for 
improving ideas and 
sometimes we have to 
change the fundamental 
concept. 
Link between 
insights and 
solutions 
 
Though we have gained 
insights we are not able to 
say exactly how our solutions 
are linked with the insights. 
We are aware that insights 
should contribute to 
solutions, but we have no 
approach to ensure that 
they do.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights. 
 
 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights and we document 
the process in order to keep 
track of how insights and 
solutions are linked. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights and continuously 
improve the approach. We 
document throughout the 
process in order to keep 
track of how the insights 
and solutions are linked.  
==PAGE:55==
Width of generated 
ideas 
 
We are uncertain whether or 
not the generated ideas cover 
the different insight areas. 
(regardless of radical ideas)  
The ideas we generate cover 
some of the different 
insight areas. (regardless of 
radical ideas) 
 
The ideas we generate cover 
most of the different insight 
areas. We cannot draw any 
value from the radical ideas 
we get. 
The ideas we generate cover 
all the different insight 
areas. We get some radical 
ideas, which we can draw 
value from. 
The ideas we generate cover 
all the different insight 
areas. We get a reasonable 
amount of radical ideas, 
which we can draw value 
from.  
Behaviour 
concerning radical 
ideas, and trust in 
the team 
 
We have a culture where 
radical ideas are not 
welcome. 
It is allowed to get radical 
ideas in a brainstorming 
session, but we rarely 
pursue them. 
Few radical ideas are 
welcome. We have to agree 
on which ideas to pursue. 
Radical ideas are welcome, 
and they can come from 
everyone. Every team 
member can pursue an idea 
that they believe in. 
Radical ideas are welcome 
and treated equal to other 
ideas. Every team member 
is encouraged to come with 
ideas and push the 
boundaries of their 
(radical) ideas.  
 
Reaction to 
disagreements  
 
We try to avoid 
disagreements or shut them 
down as quickly as possible. 
We do not see 
disagreements as 
something that can lead to 
a positive outcome, but we 
do not avoid them. 
We see disagreements as a 
sign of drive that positively 
adds to the process and 
solutions, but they are 
handled ad-hoc.  
We see disagreements as a 
sign of drive that positively 
adds to the process and 
solutions, and we have a 
few strategies to handle 
them in a constructive way.  
We see disagreements as an 
opportunity to increase the 
quality of our process and 
solutions. We have 
different strategies to 
handle them in a 
constructive way and when 
the time is right. 
Use of language and 
vocabulary for the 
design process 
 
We have a vocabulary for the 
design process, but we use it 
in our own way. We often 
struggle with 
misunderstandings 
connected to language and 
vocabulary. 
 
We have a common 
language and vocabulary 
for the design process, but 
not always certain of how 
and where to use it. Time to 
time we run into 
misunderstandings 
connected to language or 
vocabulary. 
 
We have a common 
language and vocabulary 
for the design process and 
we are certain in its use. We 
rarely have 
misunderstandings 
connected to language or 
vocabulary. 
Degree of creative 
confidence 
 
We may have ideas in the 
team, but we do not take 
action on them. 
 
We have big ideas, but we 
don’t take action on them. 
 
We believe in big ideas-no 
fear, lot’s of action from 
everyone.

==PAGE:87==
A MATURITY MODEL FOR TEAMS ADVANCING IN DESIGN THINKING 
 
0 
1 
2 
3 
4 
5 
Score 
Aim 
Understanding 
and use of 
design methods 
 
We have knowledge of  design 
methods, and have tried to 
use them in a facilitated 
context OR we have not tried 
to use them. 
We have used design methods 
in our own work, but are still 
following the procedure 
closely. 
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
methods to solve specific 
challenges in a development 
process. We are vocal and 
explicit in the use of methods 
as they are not entirely 
ingrained yet. 
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
methods to solve specific 
challenges in a development 
process. We use design 
methods as an ingrained and 
natural part of our 
development process.  
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
methods to solve specific 
challenges in a development 
process. We use design 
methods as an ingrained and 
natural part of our 
development process. We 
continuously adapt and 
improve on the methods. 
 
 
Mindset 
awareness 
 
We look for a solution 
straight away when we have a 
new problem. 
We understand the 
importance of exploring  the 
problem in order to be able to 
find the right solution. 
We spend some time to 
understand the problem, and 
then work on solutions. 
We move iteratively between 
working with the problem 
and solutions.  
We move freely and 
iteratively between working 
with the problem and 
solutions.  
 
 
 
Breadth in 
information 
gathering 
 
We gather information about 
users in an ad-hoc manner. 
We obtain some 
understanding of the users. 
We gather information from a 
few sources e.g. user research, 
market data and 
observations. We obtain some 
understanding of the users. 
We gather information from 
different sources e.g. user 
research, market data and 
observations. We obtain some 
understanding of the users’ 
behaviour, needs and 
preferences.  
We gather information from a 
broad range of sources e.g. 
user research, market data 
and observations. We mostly 
obtain a fulfilling 
understanding of the users’ 
behaviour, needs and 
preferences.  
We systematically gather 
information from a broad 
range of sources e.g. user 
research, market data and 
observations. We obtain a 
fulfilling understanding of the 
users’ behaviour, needs and 
preferences.  
 
 
Link between 
insights and 
information  
 
 
Though we have gathered 
information we are not able 
to say exactly how our 
insights are linked with the 
information. 
We are aware that insights 
should be drawn from 
information, but we have no 
approach to ensure that they 
do.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
information. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
information and we 
document the process in 
order to keep track of how 
information and insights are 
linked. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
information and continuously 
improve the approach. We 
document throughout the 
process in order to keep track 
of how the information and 
insights are linked.  
 
 
Use of 
visual/physical 
representations 
 
We rarely make 
visual/physical 
representations. The first 
tangible is the final prototype. 
 
We make visual/physical 
representations to support 
communication and facilitate 
exploration of the solution 
space. 
 
We make visual/physical 
representations throughout 
the process as a natural way 
to support communication 
and facilitate the shift 
between abstract and 
concrete levels in exploring 
the solution space.

fY9Yf
iRRI pl
==PAGE:88==
Testing  
 
We only use testing when we 
have developed a more or less 
finished solution. 
We use testing to learn before 
initiating a development 
process and when we have 
developed a more or less 
finished solution.  
We use testing throughout 
the development process. We 
validate one part of the 
solution at a time and add it 
to the final solution. 
We use testing throughout 
the development process. We 
validate new parts of the 
solution alone and in 
combination with the entire 
system of the solution.  
We use feedback to improve 
ideas and sometimes the 
fundamental concepts. 
We use testing by forming 
hypotheses about the solution 
and testing them as cheap 
and early as possible and we 
use it continuously 
throughout the development 
process. Feedback are seen as 
learning points for improving 
ideas and sometimes we have 
to change the fundamental 
concept. 
 
 
Link between 
insights and 
solutions 
 
Though we have gained 
insights we are not able to say 
exactly how our solutions are 
linked with the insights. 
We are aware that insights 
should contribute to 
solutions, but we have no 
approach to ensure that they 
do.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights. 
 
 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights and we document the 
process in order to keep track 
of how insights and solutions 
are linked. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights and continuously 
improve the approach. We 
document throughout the 
process in order to keep track 
of how the insights and 
solutions are linked.  
 
 
Generation of 
alternative 
solutions 
 
We struggle with generating 
any genuinely new alternative 
solutions. 
 
We generate a few genuinely 
new alternative solutions. 
 
We generate a reasonable 
amount of genuinely new 
alternative solutions. 
 
 
Creative 
confidence of 
the team 
 
We find it hard to believe in 
the team’s ability to create big 
ideas that solve problems 
better than existing ones. 
 
We believe in the team’s 
ability to create big ideas, that 
solve problems better than 
existing ones. We have to 
agree on which ideas can be 
pursued. 
 
We believe in the individual 
team member’s and the 
team’s ability to create big 
ideas, that solve problems 
better than existing ones. 
Individuals have the freedom 
to pursue ideas.

A MATURITY MODEL FOR TEAMS ADVANCING IN DESIGN THINKING 
 
0 
1 
2 
3 
4 
5 
Score 
Aim 
Understanding 
and use of 
design thinking 
methods 
 
We have knowledge of  design 
thinking methods, and have 
tried to use them in a 
facilitated context OR we 
have not tried to use them. 
We have used design thinking 
methods  in our own work, 
but are still following the 
procedure closely. 
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
thinking methods to solve 
specific challenges in a 
development process. We are 
vocal and explicit in the use of 
methods as they are not 
entirely ingrained yet. 
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
thinking methods to solve 
specific challenges in a 
development process. We use 
design thinking methods as 
an ingrained and natural part 
of our development process.  
We know how to select and 
apply relevant design 
thinking methods to solve 
specific challenges in a 
development process. We use 
design thinking methods as 
an ingrained and natural part 
of our development process. 
We continuously adapt and 
improve on the methods. 
 
 
Process 
approach 
 
We look for a solution 
straight away when we have a 
new problem. 
We understand the 
importance of exploring  the 
problem in order to be able to 
find the right solution. 
We spend some time to 
understand the problem, and 
then work on solutions. 
We move iteratively between 
working with the problem 
and solutions.  
We move freely and 
iteratively between working 
with the problem and 
solutions.  
 
 
 
Breadth in 
information 
gathering 
 
We gather information about 
stakeholders in an ad-hoc 
manner.  
We gather information from a 
few sources e.g. stakeholder 
research, market data and 
technology research.  
We gather information from 
different sources e.g. 
stakeholder research, market 
data and technology research.  
We gather information from a 
broad range of sources e.g. 
stakeholder research, market 
data and technology research.  
We systematically gather 
information from a broad 
range of sources e.g. 
stakeholder research, market 
data and technology research.  
 
 
Empathy 
 
We have identified our 
stakeholders. 
We obtain some 
understanding of the 
stakeholders. 
 
We obtain some 
understanding of the 
stakeholders’ behaviour, 
needs and preferences. 
We mostly obtain a fulfilling 
understanding of the 
stakeholders’ behaviour, 
needs and preferences. 
We obtain a fulfilling 
understanding of the 
stakeholders’ behaviour, 
needs and preferences.  
 
 
Link between 
insights and 
information  
 
 
Though we have gathered 
information we are not able 
to say exactly how our 
insights are linked with the 
information. 
We are aware that insights 
should be drawn from 
information, but we have no 
approach to ensure that they 
do.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
information. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
information and we keep 
track of how information and 
insights are linked. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
insights are based on 
information and continuously 
improve the approach. We 
keep track throughout the 
process of how the 
information and insights are 
linked.  
 
 
4:
e T@c3 Bp A 2qInjCRN
eYlYS
iRRI qk
==PAGE:95==
Link between 
insights and 
solutions 
 
Though we have gained 
insights we are not able to say 
exactly how our solutions are 
linked with the insights. 
We are aware that insights 
should contribute to 
solutions, but we have no 
approach to ensure that they 
do.  
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights. 
 
 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights and we keep track of 
how insights and solutions 
are linked. 
We have a systematic 
approach to ensure that our 
solutions are based on 
insights and continuously 
improve the approach. We 
keep track throughout the 
process of how the insights 
and solutions are linked.  
 
 
Use of 
visual/physical 
representations 
 
We rarely make 
visual/physical 
representations. We normally 
make a visual/physical 
prototype when we have 
finalised the solution.  
 
We make visual/physical 
representations to support 
communication and facilitate 
exploration of the solution 
space. 
 
We make visual/physical 
representations throughout 
the process as a natural way 
to support communication 
and facilitate the shift 
between abstract and 
concrete levels in exploring 
the solution space.  
 
 
Testing  
 
We only use testing when we 
have developed a more or less 
finished solution. 
We use testing to learn before 
initiating a development 
process and when we have 
developed a more or less 
finished solution.  
We use testing throughout 
the development process. We 
validate one part of the 
solution at a time and add it 
to the final solution. 
We use testing throughout 
the development process. We 
validate new parts of the 
solution alone and in 
combination with the entire 
system of the solution.  
We use feedback to improve 
ideas and sometimes the 
fundamental concepts. 
We use testing by forming 
hypotheses about the solution 
and testing them as cheap 
and early as possible and we 
use it continuously 
throughout the development 
process. Feedback are seen as 
learning points for improving 
ideas and sometimes we have 
to change the fundamental 
concept. 
 
 
Generation of 
alternative 
solutions 
 
We struggle with generating 
any genuinely new alternative 
solutions. 
 
We generate a few genuinely 
new alternative solutions. 
 
We generate a reasonable 
amount of genuinely new 
alternative solutions. 
 
 
Mindset 
 
We have some   trust in the 
team’s ability to create big 
ideas that solve problems 
better than existing ones. 
 
We believe in the team’s 
ability to create big ideas, that 
solve problems better than 
existing ones. We trust each 
other and can share most of 
our ideas in the team. 
 
We strongly believe in the 
team’s ability to create big 
ideas, that solve problems 
better than existing ones. We 
trust each other and can 
share all our (crazy) ideas in 
the team.

==PAGE:130==
Arbejde med parametre 
 
I har fået udleveret en liste af parametre som vi har lavet på baggrund af interviews og sidste 
workshop. Denne øvelse går ud på at arbejde med de parametre og forbedre listen. Læs 
gerne hele øvelsesbeskrivelsen igennem før du går i gang. I har 15-20 minutter til øvelsen. 
TAK :)  
 
1.
Listen af parametre skal ​dække alle relevante områder​ af design thinking for at man 
kan vurdere et teams design thinking capability (eller modenhed). Ud fra princippet: 
collectively exhaustive 
a.
Tilføj det du synes der mangler for at opfylde dette og fjern dem som du ikke 
finder relevante.  
b.
Skriv også alle de kommentarer du måtte have til parametrene på post-its 
eller i margen så vi får dem med. 
2.
Parametrene skal være ​uafhængige​. Dvs. at vurderingen på én parameter ikke må 
medføre en specifik vurdering på en anden parameter. Ud fra princippet: ​mutually 
exclusive. 
a.
Du må lægge parametre sammen, omformulere dem eller fjerne hvis du 
finder nogle afhængigheder. Skriv evt. kommentarer du måtte have. 
3.
Parametrene skal være ​meningsfulde​ og teamet skal kunne ​vurdere sig selv​ på dem. 
a.
Split eller saml de parametre som ikke er på det rette abstraktionsniveau. 
b.
Omformuler eller skriv kommentarer hvis der er parametre som ikke giver 
mening. 
4.
Har du andre kommentarer til parametre skal du endelig skrive dem ned.

Y:Yl

==PAGE:131==
PARAMETERS
EXPLANATION 
Method/tool Understanding 
and Use  
Being able to choose the right method, use it 
right and get the correct result. 
Width in the Data Collection 
The extent to which the team collect data that 
represents the relevant stakeholders in the 
right amount.  
Level of Systematic in the 
Data Collection 
How systematic are the team’s approach to 
data gathering? Making sure that the they get 
the kind of data that they need. 
Objectivity (in questions) 
The team must be neutral/objective towards 
the people that they are asking (interview, 
survey, focus group..) and towards the problem 
at hand. 
Link between data and 
insights 
Are the insights based on data? 
(Re)Action to a new 
Problem 
The desired action is that they explore the 
problem in a divergent manner (discover 
phase). 
Creative Confidence 
How much courage do the individuals in the 
team have to create? And to fail? 
Use of Double Diamond 
Are they using the DD? 
Teamwork environment  
The desired environment for DT 
Response to radical ideas 
Is there room for radical ideas and thoughts?  
Empathy  
The ability to put yourself in other people's 
place.  
Prototyping 
Time to first prototype and do they use 
prototyping correctly? 
Room for disagreement and 
discussions 
The ability to foster an environment where 
questions, disagreement and discussions are 
seen as steps towards generating new and 
better solutions. 
Trust within the team 
Are every person in the team allowed to 
explore a (crazy) idea that she/he believes in? 
Does every team member feel that they can do 
that? Do they trust the others enough to let 
them do that? 
Everyone’s opinions 
weighs/counts equally 
Is there a common language and equality that 
makes people share knowledge and new ideas

PARAMETERS 
 
 
 
EXPLANATION 
1 
Method/tool understanding and 
use  
Select suitable methods corresponding to the 
given stage, use them properly and draw valid 
insights from the findings.  
2 
Making ideas tangible or visual 
 
Are the team developing tangible or visuals 
aids/models/prototypes/mockups (in order to 
better understand ideas and support 
communication and the creative process)  
3 
Learning through testing in an 
iterative manner 
How does the team use testing?  
When are hypotheses/ideas tested and how 
systematic are the approach to the testing? 
Are there continuous development from the 
feedback and learnings in an iterative way. 
4 
Mindset awareness 
(Div./Con.) 
How the team works with divergent and 
convergent phases and the problem.  
5 
Width in the data/observations 
gathering 
The extent to which the team collect data that 
represents the relevant stakeholders in the 
right amount.  
6 
Objectivity in the 
data/observations gathering 
The team must be neutral/objective towards 
the people that they are asking (interview, 
survey, focus group..) and towards the 
problem at hand. 
7 
Correlation between 
data/observations and insights 
Are the insights based on data? 
data/observations/information/knowledge 
8 
Correlation between insights and 
solutions 
To what extent have the insights been used in 
the solution? 
9 
Width of ideas (span) 
How broad is the span of ideas in the team’s 
idea generations?  
 
(Innovative/DT) Team culture 
The desired environment for DT 
 This is not a parameter but a headline.  
10 
Diversity in the team (roles and 
responsibility) 
Understanding the need for facilitation, 
“deciders”, “visionaries”, “time keepers” and  
“gate keepers”. To what degree/extent does 
the team contain the needed roles for DT? Are 
all needed roles filled? Is there a hustler, 
hipster and hacker. Are there a leader than 
can be design coach 
11 
Response to radical ideas / Trust 
within the team 
Is there room for radical ideas and thoughts?  
Are every person in the team allowed to 
explore a (crazy) idea that she/he believes in? 
Does every team member feel that they can 
do that? Do they trust the others enough to let 
them do that?

Y9Yk

==PAGE:155==
12 
Empathy  
The ability to put yourself in other people's 
place. In order to be able to better understand 
their possibilities and needs.  
13 
Attitude/behaviour towards 
discussion and conflicting views 
The way questions, discussion, disagreement  
are seen. Is it something that the team is open 
towards, or something that should be shot 
down.  
14 
Common language & vocabulary 
Does the team have a common language and 
vocabulary regarding the design process? 
15 
Creative confidence in team 
Do they believe in themselves and are they 
comfortable with making mistakes? 
The ability to think big and act on ideas. Try 
different things without fear of failure. 
16 
Ambiguity 
Is the team aware of and have they embraced 
that they DO NOT KNOW what is going to 
happen and where they end 
17 
Engagement and excitement 
Is everyone equally involved and excited.

*​Only few ideas are generated, they are

solutions. No far-out ideas.

person.

include both the ‘obvious’ solutions and 
extreme, ‘unrealistic’ proposals, dream 
scenarios. 
 
Ideas are experimenting, lie in different 
directions. Solution space is broad
